<tbody><tr>
<td style="width:50%; text-align:left;"><b><a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="Speaker of the United States House of Representatives">Speaker</a> before election</b><br/>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_W._Taylor_(politician)" title="John W. Taylor (politician)">John W. Taylor</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/Democratic-Republican_Party" title="Democratic-Republican Party">Democratic-Republican</a>
</p>
</td>
<td style="width:50%; text-align:right;"><b>Elected <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="Speaker of the United States House of Representatives">Speaker</a></b> <br/>
<p><a href="/wiki/Philip_Pendleton_Barbour" title="Philip Pendleton Barbour">Philip Barbour</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/Democratic-Republican_Party" title="Democratic-Republican Party">Democratic-Republican</a>
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Elections to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a></b> for the <a href="/wiki/17th_United_States_Congress" title="17th United States Congress">17th Congress</a> took place in the various states between July 3, 1820 (<a href="#Louisiana">Louisiana</a>) and August 10, 1821 (<a href="#Tennessee">Tennessee</a>). In four states (<a href="#Illinois">Illinois</a>, <a href="#Indiana">Indiana</a>, <a href="#Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, <a href="#Mississippi">Mississippi</a>) the election coincided with the taking of the <a href="/wiki/1820_United_States_Census" title="1820 United States Census">4th Census</a> (August 7, 1820). Future enumerations would henceforth be held at a different time of year.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/James_Monroe" title="James Monroe">James Monroe</a> won reelection and the <a href="/wiki/Era_of_Good_Feelings" title="Era of Good Feelings">Era of Good Feelings</a>, a period of near-complete dominance of national politics by the Democratic-Republican Party, continued after this campaign.  However, the Democratic-Republicans lost a small number of seats, due to growing discontent in some urban, eastern areas.  However, the huge Democratic-Republican majority remained intact and the Federalist Party started to become increasingly fragmented.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_elections">Special elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1820_and_1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Special elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_special_elections_to_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="List of special elections to the United States House of Representatives">List of special elections to the United States House of Representatives</a></div>
<p>There were special elections in 1820 and 1821 to the <a href="/wiki/16th_United_States_Congress" title="16th United States Congress">16th United States Congress</a> and <a href="/wiki/17th_United_States_Congress" title="17th United States Congress">17th United States Congress</a>.
</p><p>Special elections are sorted by date then district.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="16th_Congress">16th Congress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1820_and_1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 16th Congress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<td style="background-color:#AACC99">Incumbent resigned July 6, 1820.<br/>New member <a href="/wiki/1820_Virginia%27s_1st_congressional_district_special_election" title="1820 Virginia's 1st congressional district special election">elected</a> <b>sometime in 1820</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VA1_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-VA1-15">[6]</a></sup><br/><b>Democratic-Republican gain</b>.<br/>Successor seated November 13, 1820.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16th_Roster_12-4"><a href="#cite_note-16th_Roster-12">[3]</a></sup><br/>Successor later re-elected in the April 1821 election to the next term, <a href="#Virginia">see below</a>.
</td>

<td style="background:#BBBBBB">Incumbent died December 20, 1820.<br/>New member <a href="/wiki/1821_North_Carolina%27s_4th_congressional_district_special_election" title="1821 North Carolina's 4th congressional district special election">elected</a> <b>February 7, 1821</b>.<br/>Democratic-Republican hold.<br/>Successor seated February 7, 1821.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16th_Roster_12-14"><a href="#cite_note-16th_Roster-12">[3]</a></sup><br/>Successor later re-elected in the August 9, 1821 election to the next term, <a href="#North_Carolina">see below</a>.
</td>

Blackledge</a></b> (Democratic-Republican) 57.7%</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Connecticut">Connecticut</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1820_and_1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Connecticut">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_election_in_Connecticut" title="1821 United States House of Representatives election in Connecticut">1821 United States House of Representatives election in Connecticut</a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Kentucky">Kentucky</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1820_and_1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Kentucky">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1820_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections_in_Kentucky" title="1820 United States House of Representatives elections in Kentucky">1820 United States House of Representatives elections in Kentucky</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1820_Kentucky%27s_6th_congressional_district_special_election" title="1820 Kentucky's 6th congressional district special election">1820 Kentucky's 6th congressional district special election</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1820_Kentucky%27s_9th_congressional_district_special_election" title="1820 Kentucky's 9th congressional district special election">1820 Kentucky's 9th congressional district special election</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1821_Kentucky%27s_7th_congressional_district_special_election" title="1821 Kentucky's 7th congressional district special election">1821 Kentucky's 7th congressional district special election</a>, <a href="/wiki/1821_Kentucky%27s_8th_congressional_district_special_election" title="1821 Kentucky's 8th congressional district special election">1821 Kentucky's 8th congressional district special election</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Kentucky" title="List of United States Representatives from Kentucky">List of United States Representatives from Kentucky</a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Maine">Maine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1820_and_1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Maine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1820%E2%80%931821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections_in_Maine" title="1820–1821 United States House of Representatives elections in Maine">1820–1821 United States House of Representatives elections in Maine</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1820_Maine%27s_1st_congressional_district_special_election" title="1820 Maine's 1st congressional district special election">1820 Maine's 1st congressional district special election</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Maine" title="List of United States Representatives from Maine">List of United States Representatives from Maine</a></div>
<p>This was the first election in <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a> since its separation from <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>. In the previous election, Massachusetts had had 20 representatives. Seven seats (representing the <span data-sort-value="Massachusetts14 !"><a href="/wiki/Massachusetts%27s_14th_congressional_district" title="Massachusetts's 14th congressional district">14th</a></span>-<span data-sort-value="Massachusetts20 !"><a href="/wiki/Massachusetts%27s_20th_congressional_district" title="Massachusetts's 20th congressional district">20th districts</a></span>) were reassigned from Massachusetts to Maine. In addition, under the terms of the law which admitted Maine to the union, any vacancies in the 16th Congress by Representatives elected to represent Massachusetts but residing in the new states of Maine would be filled by a resident of Maine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16th_Roster_12-15"><a href="#cite_note-16th_Roster-12">[3]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Holmes_(U.S._politician)" title="John Holmes (U.S. politician)">John Holmes</a>, who had been elected to the House for the former <span data-sort-value="Massachusetts14 !"><a href="/wiki/Massachusetts%27s_14th_congressional_district" title="Massachusetts's 14th congressional district">14th district of Massachusetts</a></span> was elected as one of the first two senators for Maine. The vacancy was filled in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1820_Maine%27s_1st_congressional_district_special_election" title="1820 Maine's 1st congressional district special election">a special election</a> by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Dane" title="Joseph Dane">Joseph Dane</a> (Federalist). Dane was the only Representative officially considered as representing Maine in the 16th Congress. The Representatives from the 15th-20th districts were still classified as being from Massachusetts for the remainder of the 16th Congress.
</p><p>Maine elected its members on November 7, 1820. Maine law required a majority to win an election, necessitating additional ballots if a majority was not received, so additional ballots were held on January 22, 1821 and September 10, 1821, after the term began but before the new Congress convened.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1820_and_1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Massachusetts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1820%E2%80%931821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections_in_Massachusetts" title="1820–1821 United States House of Representatives elections in Massachusetts">1820–1821 United States House of Representatives elections in Massachusetts</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/1820_Massachusetts%27s_1st_congressional_district_special_election" title="1820 Massachusetts's 1st congressional district special election">1820 Massachusetts's 1st congressional district special election</a>, <a href="/wiki/1820_Massachusetts%27s_8th_congressional_district_special_election" title="1820 Massachusetts's 8th congressional district special election">1820 Massachusetts's 8th congressional district special election</a>, <a href="/wiki/1820_Massachusetts%27s_13th_congressional_district_special_election" title="1820 Massachusetts's 13th congressional district special election">1820 Massachusetts's 13th congressional district special election</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Massachusetts" title="List of United States Representatives from Massachusetts">List of United States Representatives from Massachusetts</a></div>
<p>This was the first election in Massachusetts after the separation of the former <a href="/wiki/District_of_Maine" title="District of Maine">District of Maine</a> as the new State of Maine, taking the old <span data-sort-value="Massachusetts14 !"><a href="/wiki/Massachusetts%27s_14th_congressional_district" title="Massachusetts's 14th congressional district">14th</a></span> – <span data-sort-value="Massachusetts20 !"><a href="/wiki/Massachusetts%27s_20th_congressional_district" title="Massachusetts's 20th congressional district">20th</a></span> districts with it.
</p><p>Massachusetts elected its members November 6, 1820. Massachusetts had a majority requirement for election, which was not met in the <span data-sort-value="Massachusetts02 !"><a href="/wiki/Massachusetts%27s_2nd_congressional_district" title="Massachusetts's 2nd congressional district">2nd district</a></span> necessitating two additional elections on January 8, 1821 and April 16, 1821, after the term began but before the new Congress convened.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Jersey">New Jersey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1820_and_1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: New Jersey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1820_United_States_House_of_Representatives_election_in_New_Jersey" title="1820 United States House of Representatives election in New Jersey">1820 United States House of Representatives election in New Jersey</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/1820_New_Jersey%27s_at-large_congressional_district_special_election" title="1820 New Jersey's at-large congressional district special election">1820 New Jersey's at-large congressional district special election</a>, <a href="/wiki/1821_New_Jersey%27s_at-large_congressional_district_special_election" title="1821 New Jersey's at-large congressional district special election">1821 New Jersey's at-large congressional district special election</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_New_Jersey" title="List of United States Representatives from New Jersey">List of United States Representatives from New Jersey</a></div>
<p>New Jersey elected its members November 7, 1820.  There were an unusually large number of candidates, 119 candidates according to one contemporary newspaper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Jersey_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_Jersey-32">[19]</a></sup> Some candidates ran under an "Anti-Caucus" ticket.  Only 1 of the 6 six incumbents would serve in the next term, as 4 retired and 1 died after re-election.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="New_York">New York</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1820_and_1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: New York">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections_in_New_York" title="1821 United States House of Representatives elections in New York">1821 United States House of Representatives elections in New York</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/1821_New_York%27s_6th_congressional_district_special_election" title="1821 New York's 6th congressional district special election">1821 New York's 6th congressional district special election</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_New_York" title="List of United States Representatives from New York">List of United States Representatives from New York</a></div>
<p>New York elected its members April 24–26, 1821, after the term began but before the new Congress convened.  The <span data-sort-value="New York21 !"><a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_21st_congressional_district" title="New York's 21st congressional district">21st district</a></span>, previously a <a href="/wiki/Plural_district" title="Plural district">plural district</a> with two seats, was divided into two single-member districts for the 17th Congress, the 21st and <span data-sort-value="New York22 !"><a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_22nd_congressional_district" title="New York's 22nd congressional district">22nd</a></span>.
</p><p>The Democratic-Republican party in New York was divided between "Bucktails" and "<a href="/wiki/DeWitt_Clinton" title="DeWitt Clinton">Clintonians</a>". The Clintonians ran on a joint ticket with the remaining Federalists. In a few cases, marked as "Clintonian/Federalist" below, it is unclear whether a candidate on the joint ticket was Democratic-Republican or Federalist.
</p><p>Only five of the twenty-seven incumbents were re-elected to the next term.  Sixteen incumbents retired and five lost re-election.  Despite this high turnover of membership, there was only a one-seat net gain for the Federalists.
</p>

<td style="background:#BBBBBB">Incumbent retired.<br/>New member elected.<br/>Democratic-Republican hold.<br/>Successor died September 7, 1821, before the Congress convened, leading to a <a href="/wiki/1821_New_York%27s_6th_congressional_district_special_election" title="1821 New York's 6th congressional district special election">November 6–8, 1821 special election</a>.

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Carolina">North Carolina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1820_and_1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: North Carolina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections_in_North_Carolina" title="1821 United States House of Representatives elections in North Carolina">1821 United States House of Representatives elections in North Carolina</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/1821_North_Carolina%27s_4th_congressional_district_special_election" title="1821 North Carolina's 4th congressional district special election">1821 North Carolina's 4th congressional district special election</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_North_Carolina" title="List of United States Representatives from North Carolina">List of United States Representatives from North Carolina</a></div>
<p>North Carolina elected its members August 9, 1821, after the term began but before the new Congress convened.

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tennessee">Tennessee</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1820_and_1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tennessee">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections_in_Tennessee" title="1821 United States House of Representatives elections in Tennessee">1821 United States House of Representatives elections in Tennessee</a></div>

<p>Tennessee elected its members August 9–10, 1821, after the term began but before the new Congress convened.

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vermont">Vermont</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1820_and_1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Vermont">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1820%E2%80%931821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections_in_Vermont" title="1820–1821 United States House of Representatives elections in Vermont">1820–1821 United States House of Representatives elections in Vermont</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Vermont" title="List of United States Representatives from Vermont">List of United States Representatives from Vermont</a></div>
<p>In 1820, Vermont returned to using districts. This would be the only election in which the <span data-sort-value="Vermont06 !"><a href="/wiki/Vermont%27s_6th_congressional_district" title="Vermont's 6th congressional district">6th district</a></span> would be used.
</p><p>Vermont elected its members September 5, 1820.  A majority was required for election, which was not met in the 2nd or 3rd district, requiring additional ballots to achieve a majority. The 2nd district required 7 ballots. The 3rd district required two additional ballots.  The additional ballots were held December 11, 1820, and February 19, May 1, July 2, September 4, and October 22, 1821.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Virginia">Virginia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1820_and_1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Virginia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections_in_Virginia" title="1821 United States House of Representatives elections in Virginia">1821 United States House of Representatives elections in Virginia</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/1820_Virginia%27s_1st_congressional_district_special_election" title="1820 Virginia's 1st congressional district special election">1820 Virginia's 1st congressional district special election</a>, <a href="/wiki/1820_Virginia%27s_10th_congressional_district_special_election" title="1820 Virginia's 10th congressional district special election">1820 Virginia's 10th congressional district special election</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1820_Virginia%27s_17th_congressional_district_special_election" title="1820 Virginia's 17th congressional district special election">1820 Virginia's 17th congressional district special election</a>, <a href="/wiki/1820_Virginia%27s_20th_congressional_district_special_election" title="1820 Virginia's 20th congressional district special election">1820 Virginia's 20th congressional district special election</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Virginia" title="List of United States Representatives from Virginia">List of United States Representatives from Virginia</a></div>
<p>Virginia elected its members in April 1821, after the term began but before the new Congress convened.

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-voting_delegates">Non-voting delegates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1820_and_1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Non-voting delegates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There were four territories that had the right to send a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delegate_(United_States_Congress)" title="Delegate (United States Congress)">delegate</a> to at least part of the 17th Congress, only three of which actually sent delegates. <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Territory" title="Missouri Territory">Missouri Territory</a>'s seat remained vacant, as the territory was admitted as the State of Missouri early in the 17th Congress.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-Gorham-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Gorham_18-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Gorham_18-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Gorham_18-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Gorham_18-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Gorham_18-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"> Some sources cite <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Gorham" title="Benjamin Gorham">Benjamin Gorham</a> as a Federalist.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-nr-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-9"><sup><i><b>j</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-10"><sup><i><b>k</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-11"><sup><i><b>l</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-12"><sup><i><b>m</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-13"><sup><i><b>n</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-14"><sup><i><b>o</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-15"><sup><i><b>p</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-16"><sup><i><b>q</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nr_24-17"><sup><i><b>r</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"> Source does not give numbers of votes or has incomplete data.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> In <span data-sort-value="Maryland06 !"><a href="/wiki/Maryland%27s_6th_congressional_district" title="Maryland's 6th congressional district">Maryland's 6th district</a></span>, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Reed" title="Philip Reed">Philip Reed</a> later successfully contested the tie, claiming 7 votes for him that had not been counted,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[18]</a></sup> and was seated March 22, 1822.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17th_Roster_23-8"><a href="#cite_note-17th_Roster-23">[13]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> District numbers differed between source used and elsewhere on Wikipedia; district numbers used elsewhere on Wikipedia used here.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-NY01-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-NY01_33-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-NY01_33-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-NY01_33-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-NY01_33-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-NY01_33-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"> In <span data-sort-value="New York01 !"><a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_1st_congressional_district" title="New York's 1st congressional district">New York's 1st district</a></span>, the winners were initially declared to be <a href="/wiki/Silas_Wood" title="Silas Wood">Silas Wood</a> (Federalist) and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sharpe" title="Peter Sharpe">Peter Sharpe</a> (Democratic-Republican). Sharpe's election <a href="/wiki/1821_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections_in_New_York#Aftermath,_special_elections_and_contested_election" title="1821 United States House of Representatives elections in New York">was challenged</a>. Initial returns showed 3,339 votes for <a href="/wiki/Cadwallader_D._Colden" title="Cadwallader D. Colden">Cadwallader D. Colden</a> (Federalist), with 395 for "Cadwallader Colden" and 220 for "Cadwallader D. Colder". After those votes were declared to be for Cadwallader D. Colden, he finished in 2nd place with 3,954 votes (27.1%), and thus received one of the two seats for that district in place of Sharpe.  He was seated December 12, 1821.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17th_Roster_23-10"><a href="#cite_note-17th_Roster-23">[13]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-inc-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-inc_34-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-inc_34-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-inc_34-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-inc_34-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"> Based on incomplete returns</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> <a href="/wiki/John_Sergeant_(politician)" title="John Sergeant (politician)">John Sergeant</a> was also supported by the Democratic-Republicans.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-pc-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-pc_36-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-pc_36-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-pc_36-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"> Changed parties</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> <a href="/wiki/Job_Durfee" title="Job Durfee">Job Durfee</a> received votes in many towns from Federalists.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
